MIP2, of 247 aas and 6 TMSs.<br /></span></p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>MIP2 of <em>Chlamydomonas reinhardtii (Chlamydomonas smithii)</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.4"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.4&tcname=">1.A.8.8.4</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp6 aquaporin (also transports NO<sub>3</sub><sup>-</sup> and other anions at acidic pH or in the presence of Hg<sup>2+</sup>) (<span id="ref2348.12177001" class="cite">Ikeda <em>et al</em>., 2002</span>). AQP6 flicker rapidly between closed and open states. Two well conserved glycine residues: Gly-57 in TMS 2 and Gly-173 in TMS 5 reside at the contact point where the two helices cross. Mammalian orthologs of AQP6 have an asparagine residue (Asn-60) at the position corresponding to Gly-57 in Aqp6. <span id="ref34550658.15671159" class="cite">Liu <em>et al.</em> 2005 </span>showed that a single residue substitution (N60G in rat AQP6) eliminates anion permeability but increases water permeability.</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp6 of <em>Homo sapiens</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.5"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.5&tcname=">1.A.8.8.5</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p><a></a></p>
<p><!-- test--></p>
<p><a></a></p>
<p>Aquaporin-4 (AQP4) is the major water channel in the central nervous system and plays an important role in the brain's water balance, including edema formation and clearance. There are 6 splice variants; the shorter ones assemble into functional, tetrameric square arrays; the longer is palmitoylated on N-terminal cysteyl residues) (<a>Suzuki <em>et al.</em>, 2008</a>). The longest, Aqp4e, has a novel N-terminal domain and forms a water channel in the plasma membrane although various shorter variants don't (<a>Moe <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>). AQP4, like AQP0 (1.A.8.8.2), forms water channels but also forms adhesive junctions (<a>Engel <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>) (causes cytotoxic brain swelling in mice (<a>Yang <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>)) Mice lacking Aqp4 have impaired olfactions (<a>Lu <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>). Aqp4 is down regulated in skeletal muscle in muscular dystrophy (<span>Au <em>et al.</em> 2008</span>). The crystal structure is known to 2.8 &Aring; resolution (<a>Tani <em>et al.</em>, 2009</a>). The structure reveals 8 water molecules in each of the four channels, supporting a hydrogen-bond isolation mechanism and explains its fast and selective water conduction and proton exclusion (<a>Tani <em>et al.</em>, 2009</a>; <a>Cui and Bastien, 2011</a>). It is an important antigen in Neuromyelitis optica (NMO) patients (<a>Kalluri <em>et al.,</em> 2011</a>).&nbsp; A connection has been made between AQP4-mediated fluid accumulation and post traumatic syringomyelia (<span>Hemley <em>et al.</em> 2013</span>).&nbsp; AQP4 has increased water
permeability at low pH, and His95 is the pH-dependent gate (<span>Kaptan <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>).&nbsp; Also transports NH<sub>3</sub> but not NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup> (<span>Assentoft <em>et al.</em> 2016</span>). Cerebellar damage following status epilepticus involves down regulation of AQP4 expression (<span>Tang <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>). SUR1-TRPM4 and AQP4 form a complex to increase bulk water influx during astrocyte swelling (<span>Stokum <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>). A mutation, S111T, causes intellectual disability, hearing loss, and progressive gait dysfunction (<span>Berland <em>et al.</em> 2018</span>). As in humans, the chicken ortholog, Aqp4, is found in brain &gt; kidney &gt; stomach (<span>Ram&iacute;rez-Lorca <em>et al.</em> 2006</span>). A Molecular Dynamics Investigation on Human AQP4 has been published (<span id="ref34549369.30556005" class="cite">Marracino <em>et al.</em> 2018</span>). AQP1 and AQP4 activities correlate with the severity of hydrocephalus induced by subarachnoid haemorrhage (<span id="ref34551078.31556577" class="cite">Long <em>et al.</em> 2019</span>). Di-lysine motif-like sequences formed by deleting the C-terminal domain of aquaporin-4 prevent its trafficking to the plasma membrane (<span id="ref34552604.33474763" class="cite">Chau <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). Kidins220 deficiency causes ventriculomegaly via SNX27-retromer-dependent AQP4 degradation (<span id="ref34553320.34002021" class="cite">Del Puerto <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). AQP4 expression is upregulated in cells exposed to dexamethasone, and SUMOylation [Small ubiquitin-like modifiers (SUMOs)] may participate in this regulation (<span id="ref34553792.32495129" class="cite">Zhang <em>et al.</em> 2020</span>). Simultaneous calmodulin binding to the N- and C-terminal cytoplasmic domains of aquaporin 4 has been demonstrated (<span id="ref34554127.34890582" class="cite">Ishida <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). Aqp-4 plays a role in secondary pathological processes (spinal cord edema, glial scar formation, and inflammatory response) after spinal cord injury, SCI. Loss of AQP-4 is associated with reduced spinal edema and improved prognosis after SCI in mice, and downregulation of AQP-4 reduces glial scar formation and the inflammatory response after SCI (<span id="ref34554813.34915672" class="cite">Pan <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>). AQP4 contributes to the migration and proliferation of gliomas, and to their resistance to therapy. In glioma cell cultures, in both subcutaneous and orthotopic gliomas in rats, and in glioma tumours in patients, that transmembrane water-efflux rate is a sensitive biomarker of AQP4 expression (<span id="ref34555674.36376487" class="cite">Jia <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>). Aquaporin 4 is required for T cell receptor-mediated lymphocyte activation (<span id="ref34556114.36805947" class="cite">Nicosia <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Peripheral lung infections influence the blood brain barrier (BBB) water exchange, which appears to be mediated by endothelial dysfunction and is associated with an increase in perivascular AQP4 (<span id="ref34556401.37013549" class="cite">Ohene <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Trifluoperazine reduces apoptosis and 
inflammatory responses in traumatic brain injury by preventing the 
accumulation of Aquaporin4 on the surface of brain cells (<span id="ref34556487.37213674" class="cite">Xing <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Cation flux through SUR1-TRPM4 and NCX1 in astrocyte
 endfeet induces water influx through AQP4 and brain swelling after 
ischemic stroke (<span id="ref34556560.37279286" class="cite">Stokum <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Aquaporin-4 expression and modulation may be important in a rat model of post-traumatic syringomyelia (<span id="ref34556635.37316571" class="cite">Berliner <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).&nbsp; The Aqp4 water channel may be a drug target for Alzheimer's Disease (<span id="ref34556893.37475487" class="cite">Silverglate <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). A series of 2,4,5-trisubstituted oxazoles 3a-j were synthesized by a Lewis acid mediated reaction of aroylmethylidene malonates with nitriles. In silico studies conducted using the protein data bank (PDB) structure 3gd8 for AQP4 revealed that compound 3a would serve as a suitable candidate to inhibit AQP4 in human lung cells (NCI-H460). In vitro studies demonstrated that compound 3a could effectively inhibit AQP4 and inflammatory cytokines in lung cells, and hence it may be considered as a viable drug candidate for the treatment of various lung diseases (<span id="ref34557261.37664213" class="cite">Meenakshi <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).&nbsp;&nbsp; The effect of AQP4 and its palmitoylation on the permeability of exogenous reactive oxygen species has been considered (<span id="ref34557507.37866582" class="cite">Cao <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). ORI-TRN-002 exhibits superior solubility and overcomes free fraction 
limitations compared to other reported AQP4 inhibitors, suggesting its 
potential as a promising anti-edema therapy for treating cerebral edema (<span id="ref34557753.38255997" class="cite">Thormann <em>et al.</em> 2024</span>).&nbsp; <strong class="sub-title"> </strong> New biomarkers, such as aquaporin 4 have led to the 
identification of antigen-specific immune-mediated myelopathies and 
approved therapies to prevent disease progression (<span id="ref34557777.38330478" class="cite">Levy 2024</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>AQP4 of <em>Homo sapiens</em> (P55087)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.6"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.6&tcname=">1.A.8.8.6</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC>Aqp1 water channel of the sleeping chironomid (functions in water removal during anhydrobiosis,&nbsp;<span id="ref5022.18082130" class="cite">Kikawada et al., 2008</span>).<br /</TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp1 of <em>Polypedilum vanderplanki</em><br /> (A5A7N9)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.7"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.7&tcname=">1.A.8.8.7</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp2 water channel of the sleeping chironomid (functions in water homeostasis during anhydrobiosis (<span id="ref5022.18082130" class="cite">Kikawada <em>et al.</em>, 2008</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp2 of <em>Polypedilum vanderplanki</em> (A5A7P0)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.8"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.8&tcname=">1.A.8.8.8</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Vasopressin-sensitive aquaporin-2 (Aqp2) in the apical membrane of the renal collecting duct (<a>Fenton <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>).&nbsp; Controls cell volume and thereby influences cell proliferation (<a>Di Giusto <em>et al.</em> 2012</a>).&nbsp; It&nbsp; plays a
key role in concentrating urine. Water reabsorption is regulated by AQP2 trafficking between
intracellular storage vesicles and the apical membrane. This process is tightly controlled by the
pituitary hormone arginine vasopressin, and defective trafficking results in nephrogenic diabetes
insipidus (NDI).&nbsp; The crystal structure of Aqp2 has been solved to 2.75 &Aring; (<a>Frick <em>et al.</em> 2014</a>).&nbsp; In terrestrial vertebrates, AQP2 function is generally regulated by arginine-vasopressin to
accomplish key functions in osmoregulation such as the maintenance of body water
homeostasis by a cyclic AMP-independent mechanism (<span>Olesen and Fenton 2017</span>; <span>Martos-Sitcha <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>). AQP2 is expressed in the anterior vaginal wall and fibroblasts, and regulates the expression level of collagen I/III i, suggesting that AQP2 is associated with the pathogenesis of stress urinary incontinence through collagen metabolism during ECM remodeling (<span>Zhang <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>). As in humans, the chicken ortholog, Aqp2, is found only in the kidney (<span>Ram&iacute;rez-Lorca <em>et al.</em> 2006</span>).&nbsp; AQP2 is critical in regulating urine concentrating ability. The expression and function of AQP2 are regulated by a series of transcriptional factors and post-transcriptional phosphorylation, ubiquitination, and glycosylation (<span id="ref34549715.30654539" class="cite">He and Yang 2019</span>). Mutation or functional deficiency of AQP2 leads to severe nephrogenic diabetes insipidus, and inhibition of various aquaporins leads to many water-related diseases such as, edema, cardiac arrest, and stroke. <span id="ref34549876.31204482" class="cite">Maroli <em>et al.</em> 2019 </span>reported on the molecular mechanisms of mycotoxin (citrinin, ochratoxin-A, and T-2 mycotoxin) inhibition of AQP2 and arginine vasopressin receptor 2 (AVPR2). Aquaporin-2 mutations cause Nephrogenic diabetes insipidus (<span id="ref34553789.34512542" class="cite">Li <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). Meniere's disease is affected by dexamethasone which is a direct modulator of AQP2. The molecular mechanisms involved in dexamethasone binding to and its regulatory action upon AQP2 function have been described (<span id="ref34554646.35454100" class="cite">Mom <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>). Interaction of cortisol with aquaporin-2 modulates its water permeability (<span id="ref34555805.36675012" class="cite">Mom <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). In the kidney collecting duct, arginine vasopressin-dependent trafficking of AQP2 fine-tunes reabsorption of water from pre-urine, allowing precise regulation of the final urine volume. Point mutations in the gene for AQP2 disturbs this process and leads to nephrogenic diabetes insipidus (NDI), wherein patients void large volumes of hypo-osmotic urine. In recessive NDI, mutants of AQP2 are retained in the endoplasmic reticulum due to misfolding. The structures allow interpretation of these results (<span id="ref34557267.37674034" class="cite">Hagstr&ouml;mer <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Differential regulation of autophagy on urine-concentrating capability occurs through modulating renal AQP2 expression (<span id="ref34557371.37589054" class="cite">Xu <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp2 of <em>Homo sapiens</em> (P41181)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.8.9"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.8.9&tcname=">1.A.8.8.9</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 5 (x-ray structure at 2.0 &Aring; resolution (PDB# 3D9S) is available) (<span>Horsefield <em>et al.</em>, 2008</span>). Aqp5 is a marker for proliferation and migration of human breast cancer cells (<span>Jung <em>et al.</em>, 2011</span>). Plays a role in chronic obstructive pulmonary diseases (COPD) (<span><span>Zhao <em>et al.</em> 2014</span></span>).&nbsp; Its expression is regulated by androgens (<span>Pust <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>). As in humans, the chicken ortholog, Aqp5, is found in the intestine, the jejunum, ileum and colon (<span>Ram&iacute;rez-Lorca <em>et al.</em> 2006</span>). Proteomic analyses of the ocular lens revealed palmitoylation (<span id="ref34549744.30489624" class="cite">Wang and Schey 2018</span>). Aquaporin 5 expression correlates with tumor multiplicity and vascular invasion in hepatocellular carcinoma (<span id="ref34550827.31933856" class="cite">Vireak <em>et al.</em> 2019</span>). The ability of Aqp5 (as well as Aqp0 and Aqp1) to transport hydrogen peroxide (H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>) may cause cataracts in the eye (<span id="ref34552030.32063362" class="cite">Varadaraj and Kumari 2020</span>). AQP3 and AQP5 play important but different roles in spermatogenesis and sperm maturation in dogs (<span id="ref34552911.33744817" class="cite">Mirabella <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). The up-regulation of AQP1, AQP3 and AQP5 in skin during summer season indicates roles in thermoregulation (<span id="ref34553793.33077138" class="cite">Debbarma <em>et al.</em> 2020</span>). Aqp5 interacts with TRPV4 (see 1.A.4.2.5 for the rat ortholog) (<span id="ref34555448.36232935" class="cite">Kem&eacute;ny and Ducza 2022</span>). AQP5 facilitates osmotically driven water flux across biological membranes as well as the movement of hydrogen peroxide and CO<sub>2</sub>. Various mechanisms dynamically regulate AQP5 expression, trafficking, and function. Besides fulfilling its primary water permeability function, AQP5 regulates downstream effectors (<span id="ref34555993.36768212" class="cite">D'Agostino <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Modulation of membrane trafficking of AQP5 in 
the lens in response to changes in zonular tension is mediated by TRPV1 (<span id="ref34556534.37240426" class="cite">Petrova <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).Methazolamide reduces AQP5 mRNA expression and immune cell migration, and may be a drug for sepsis <span class="identifier pubmed"> <span class="current-id" title="PubMed ID">therapy</span><strong class="current-id" title="PubMed ID"> </strong></span>(<span id="ref34557681.38203778" class="cite">Rump <em>et al.</em> 2024</span>).&nbsp;</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 5 of <em>Homo sapiens</em> (P55064)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR><TD COLSPAN=5><B>Examples:</B><P></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD>TC#</TD><TD>Name</TD><TD>Organismal Type</TD><TD>Example</TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.1"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.1&tcname=">1.A.8.9.1</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 3. 95% identical to the human orthologue. Poorly permeable to water, but more permeable to glycerol and arsenic trioxide (<span id="ref34547365.28914342" class="cite">Palmgren <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>).&nbsp; It is expressed in the plasma membrane of basal epidermal cells in the skin; loss of function prevents skin tumorigenesis and epidermal cell proliferation (<span id="ref4473.17967887" class="cite">Hara-Chikuma and Verkman, 2008</span>).&nbsp; The human orthologue also transports both water and glycerol and is the predominant AQP in skin (<span id="ref10023.23677388" class="cite">Jungersted <em>et al.</em> 2013</span>). It's function is necessary for normal proliferation of colon cancer cells due to glycerol uptake (<span id="ref34546423.26768614" class="cite">Li <em>et al.</em> 2016</span>). Aqp3 is implicated in cancer progression to the metastatic state as its function promotes cell migration and cell shape plasticity.&nbsp; Its synthesis is regulated by the AhR (aryl hydrocarbon (pollutant) receptor or dioxin receptor), a transcription factor triggered by environmental pollutants (<span id="ref34545983.26454884" class="cite">Bui <em>et al.</em> 2016</span>). Trefoil factor (TFF) peptides increase cell water permeability and induce prodcution of Aqp3 (<span id="ref34549002.29046361" class="cite">Marchbank and Playford 2018</span>). Although AQP3 and other similar transmembrane proteins do not themselves transport drugs, changes in their expression levels can cause changes in cell membrane fluidity, thus affecting drug absorption rates (<span id="ref34549623.30925715" class="cite">Ikarashi <em>et al.</em> 2019</span>).&nbsp; AQP3 levels are elevated in human endometrioid carcinoma (<span id="ref34551463.32382899" class="cite">Watanabe <em>et al.</em> 2020</span>). AQP3 and AQP5 play important roles in spermatogenesis and sperm maturation in dogs (<span id="ref34552911.33744817" class="cite">Mirabella <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). AQP-1, 3 and 8 levels in amniotic fluid were measured in patients suffering from polyhydramnios. They were compared to the levels observed in control subjects, and their relationship with maternal factors and neonatal issues was analyzed. AQP-1, 3, 8 levels physiologically fluctuated, AQP-1 levels were the lowest and AQP-3 the highest, with a decrease at the end of pregnancy (<span id="ref34553689.34254277" class="cite">Guibourdenche <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). The human ortholog, Aqp3 (Q92482) is 95% identical. It transports water, glycerol and urea, and is the blood group antigen, GIL (<span id="ref34554903.12239222" class="cite">Roudier <em>et al.</em> 2002</span>). Intra-endolymphatic sac steroids have regulatory effects on inner ear AQP-3 expression via the vestibular aqueduct and modulate the homeostasis of endolymphatic fluids (<span id="ref34554904.14669532" class="cite">Kitahara <em>et al.</em> 2003</span>).</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 3 of <em>Rattus norvegicus </em> (P47862)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.10"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.10&tcname=">1.A.8.9.10</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp9 or Aqp-h9 of 294 aas.&nbsp; Takes up glycerol as well as water, and thereby contributes to freeze tolerance (<span>Hirota <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>). An almost identical orthologue, HC-9 in <em>Dryophytes chrysoscelis</em> (gray treefrog), similarly facilitates glycerol permeability. Both the transcriptional and translational levels of HC-9 change in response to thermal challenges, with a unique increase in liver during freezing and thawing (<span>Stogsdill <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp9 of<em> Hyla japonica</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.11"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.11&tcname=">1.A.8.9.11</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp1 of 304 aas and 6 TMSs;  the most abundant transmembrane protein in the tegument of Schistosoma mansoni.
This protein is expressed in all developmental stages and seems to be essential in parasite survival
since it plays a crucial role in osmoregulation, nutrient transport and drug uptake (<span id="ref34545490.24786243" class="cite">Figueiredo <em>et al.</em> 2014</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp1 of <em>Schistosoma mansoni</em> (Blood fluke)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.12"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.12&tcname=">1.A.8.9.12</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Basolateral Aqp3 of 292 aas and 6 TMSs in the frog urinary bladder (<span id="ref34545538.25220852" class="cite">Shibata <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of <em>Xenopus laevis</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.13"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.13&tcname=">1.A.8.9.13</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaglycerolporin, Aqp (high permeability to ammonium, methylamine, glycerol and water) (<span id="ref2800.14734807" class="cite">Beitz <em>et al</em>., 2004</span>) NH<sub>4</sub><sup>+</sup>/NH<sub>3</sub><sup>+</sup>CH<sub>3</sub>/glycerol/water transporter (<span id="ref4161.16889642" class="cite">Zeuthen <em>et al</em>., 2006</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Protozoan</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp of <em>Plasmodium falciparum</em> (CAC88373)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.14"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.14&tcname=">1.A.8.9.14</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Glycerolaquaporin 9, Aqp9 of 295 aas and 6 TMSs.&nbsp; Transports water, glycerol and arsenic trioxide, As<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (<span>Palmgren <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>) as well as urea and lactic acid (but not lactate) (<span id="ref34554399.35054513" class="cite">Geistlinger <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>). Primary APL cells express AQP9 significantly (2-3 logs) higher than other acute myeloid leukemia cells (AMLs), explaining their exquisite As<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> sensitivity (<span>Leung <em>et al.</em> 2007</span>). AQP-7 and AQP-9-mediated glycerol transport in tanycyte cells may be 
under hormonal control to use glycerol as an energy source during the 
mouse estrus cycle (<span>Yaba <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>). It transports multiple neutral and ionic arsenic species including arsenic trioxide, monomethylarsenous acid (MAs(III)) and dimethylarsenic acid (DMA(V)). It also transports clinically relevant selenium species including monomethylselenic acid (MSeA), especially at acidic pH. FCCP, valinomycin and nigericin do not significantly inhibit MSeA uptake, but AQP9 also transport ionic selenite and lactate, with low efficiency compared with MSeA uptake. Selenite and lactate uptake is pH dependent and inhibited by FCCP and nigericin but not valinomycin. The selenite and lactate uptake via AQP9 can be inhibited by different lactate analogs. AQP9 transport of MSeA, selenite and lactate is inhibited by an AQP9 inhibitor, phloretin, and the AQP9 substrate, arsenite (As(III)) (<span>Geng <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>). The host aquaporin-9 is required for efficient <em>Plasmodium falciparum</em> sporozoite entry into human hepatocytes (<span id="ref34553525.34268141" class="cite">Amanzougaghene <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>). RG100204 is a direct blocker of the AQP9 channel (<span id="ref34555550.36231080" class="cite">Florio <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font <span><span>melarsoprol and</span></span><span> </span><span>pentamidine (<span>Schmidt <em>et al.</em> 2018</span>)</span>. <p><!-- test--></p>
<p><a id="1.A.8.9.2"></a></p>
<p>Aquaporin-9 (Aqp9) (permeable to glycerol, urea, polyols, carbamides, purines, pyrmidines, nucleosides, monocarboxylates, pentavalent methylated arsenicals and the arsenic chemotherapeutic drug, trisenox (<a class="reflink" href="result.php?tc=1.A.8#ref6797">McDermott <em>et al.</em>, 2009</a>).&nbsp; It is poorly permeable to water and not permeable to &beta;-hydroxybutyrate (<a class="reflink" href="result.php?tc=1.A.8#ref2509">Carbrey <em>et al</em>., 2003</a>). (Regulated by CFTR and NHERF1 in response to cyclic AMP (<a class="reflink" href="result.php?tc=1.A.8#ref4704">Pietrement <em>et al</em>., 2008</a>)) The 7 &Aring; projection structure and a homology model revealed that pore-lining residues and the hydrophobic edge of the tripathic pore of GlpF (1.A.8.1.1) provide the basis for broad substrate specificity (<a class="reflink" href="result.php?tc=1.A.8#ref5069">Viadiu <em>et al</em>., 2007</a>).&nbsp; It is important for urea transport in mouse hepatocytes (<span id="ref9159.23042941" class="cite">Jelen <em>et al.</em> 2012</span>).&nbsp; Activation of the PPAR&alpha; transcription factor results in reduction in the abundance of
AQP9 in periportal hepatocytes, but its activation in the fed state directs glycerol into
glycerolipid synthesis rather than into de novo synthesis of glucose (<span id="ref34543763.25477377" class="cite">Lebeck <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>).&nbsp; Azacytidine up-regulates AQP9 and enhances arsenic trioxide (As<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>)-mediated
cytotoxicity in acute myeloid leukemia (AML) (<span id="ref34544013.25953102" class="cite">Chau <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>).&nbsp; Human Aqp9 transports hydrogen peroxide (HOOH) (<span id="ref34545111.26837049" class="cite">Watanabe <em>et al.</em> 2016</span>) and plays a role in certain types of cancer (<span id="ref34553731.32229502" class="cite">Zheng <em>et al.</em> 2020</span>). Human aquaporin 9 regulates Leydig cell steroidogenesis in diabetes (<span id="ref34554894.35352592" class="cite">Kannan <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp9 of <em>Rattus norvegicus</em> (P56627)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.20"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.20&tcname=">1.A.8.9.20</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin of 274 aas and 6 TMSs. See <span id="ref34548739.30221673" class="cite">Zhou <em>et al.</em> 2018</span> for its identification.</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp of <em>Blomia tropicalis</em> (mite)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.21"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.21&tcname=">1.A.8.9.21</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 3, Aqp3, of 304 aas and 6 TMSs. CCCP and gramicidin but not nigericin inhibit <em>Trypanosoma brucei</em> Aquaglyceroporins Aqp2 and Aqp3 at neutral pH (<a class="reflink" href="http://www.tcdb.org/search/result.php?tc=1.A.8#ref34552187">Petersen and Beitz 2020</a>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of <em>Trypanosoma brucei</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.22"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.22&tcname=">1.A.8.9.22</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin-3-like protein, Aqp10b, of 374 aas and 6 TMSs (<span id="ref34553867.14978062" class="cite">Santos <em>et al.</em> 2004</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp10b of <em>Sparus aurata</em> (gilthead seabream)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.23"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.23&tcname=">1.A.8.9.23</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of 294 aas and 6 TMSs (<span id="ref34554942.35678605" class="cite">Mashini <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of <em>Exaiptasia diaphana</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.24"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.24&tcname=">1.A.8.9.24</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of 292 aas and 6 TMSs. It is a water channel required to promote glycerol permeability and water transport across cell membranes (<span id="ref34554903.12239222" class="cite">Roudier <em>et al.</em> 2002</span>, <span id="ref34555382.30420639" class="cite">Gotfryd <em>et al.</em> 2018</span>). It acts
 as a glycerol transporter in skin and plays an important role in 
regulating the stratum corneum and epidermal glycerol content. It is involved
 in skin hydration, wound healing, and tumorigenesis, and it provides the kidney 
medullary collecting duct with high permeability to water, thereby 
permitting water to move in the direction of an osmotic gradient. It is slightly permeable to urea and H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, and may function as a water and urea exit 
mechanism in antidiuresis in collecting duct cells. It may play an 
important role in gastrointestinal tract water transport and in glycerol
 metabolism. Breast cancer cell invasion and metastasis are related to AQP3, which is the transmembrane transport channel for H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> molecules (<span id="ref34555383.36115652" class="cite">Zhong <em>et al.</em> 2022</span>). AQP3 plays a key role in cancer and metastasis. RoT inhibits human AQP3 activity with an IC<sub>50</sub> in the micromolar range (22.8 &plusmn; 5.8 &micro;M for water and 6.7 &plusmn; 3.0 &micro;M for
 glycerol permeability inhibition). RoT blocks AQP3-glycerol permeation by establishing 
strong and stable interactions at the extracellular region of AQP3 pores (<span id="ref34556192.36983077" class="cite">Paccetti-Alves <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). AQP3-mediated activation of the AMPK/SIRT1 
signaling pathway curtails gallstone formation in mice by inhibiting 
inflammatory injury of gallbladder mucosal epithelial cells (<span id="ref34557109.37641009" class="cite">Wang <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).&nbsp; The main subtype expressed in the epidermis and dermis is AQP3. AQPs exert certain physiological functions in the skin, such as the maintenance of normal shape, the regulation of body temperature, moisturization and hydration, anti-aging, damage repair and antigen presentation. The abnormal expression of AQPs in skin cells can lead to a variety of skin diseases (<span id="ref34557475.37823486" class="cite">Liu <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).&nbsp; AQP3 promotes the invasion and metastasis in cervical cancer by regulating NOX4-derived H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2 </sub>activation of the Syk/PI3K/Akt signaling axis. Aquaglyceroporin AQP3 is expressed in the mammalian lens (<span id="ref34557894.38354944" class="cite">Petrova <em>et al.</em> 2024</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp3 of <em>Homo sapiens</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.3"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.3&tcname=">1.A.8.9.3</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Major aquaglyceroporin, LmAQP1: transports water, glycerol, methylglyoxal, trivalent metalloids such as arsenite and antimonite, dihydroxyacetone and sugar alcohols. Also takes up the activated form or the drug, pentostam.&nbsp; It localizes to the flagellum of the <em>Leishmania </em> promastigotes and is used to regulate volume in response to hypoosmotic stress; it functions in osmotaxis (<span id="ref4036.15678148" class="cite">Figarella <em>et al</em>., 2005</span>; <span id="ref2928.15138256" class="cite">Gourbal <em>et al</em>, 2004</span>).&nbsp; The first line treatment for cutaneous leishmaniasis is pentavalent 
antimony such as sodium stibogluconate (pentostam) and meglumine 
antimonite (glucantime), and both compounds are transported by LmAQP1 (<span id="ref34551003.31673266" class="cite">Eslami <em>et al.</em> 2020</span>). The mutation G133D in the <em>Leishmania guyanensis</em> AQP1 is highly destabilizing (<span id="ref34553506.34175297" class="cite">Tunes <em>et al.</em> 2021</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Protozoa</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp1 of <em>Leishmania major</em> (Q6Q1Q6)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.4"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.4&tcname=">1.A.8.9.4</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 1 (permeable to water, glycerol, dihydroxyacetone and urea) (<span id="ref2967.15294911" class="cite">Uzcategui <em>et al</em>., 2004</span>)</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Protozoan</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp1 of <em>Trypanosoma brucei</em> (Q6ZXT4)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.5"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.5&tcname=">1.A.8.9.5</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin 10 of 301 aas and 6 TMSs. Cell- and tissue-specific expression of AQP-0, AQP-3, and AQP-10 in the testis, efferent ducts, and epididymis has been demonstrated (<span id="ref34551643.15223838" class="cite">Hermo <em>et al.</em> 2019</span>). It is also present in keratinocytes and the stratum corneum (<span id="ref10023.23677388" class="cite">Jungersted <em>et al.</em> 2013</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp10 of <em>Homo sapiens</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.6"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.6&tcname=">1.A.8.9.6</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Glycerol/water/urea/arsenic trioxide-transporting channel protein, aqaporin 7 or Aqp7, but water is a poor substrate (<span>Palmgren <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>).&nbsp; Present in adipose tissue where it allows glycerol efflux.&nbsp; Defects result in increased accumulation of triglycerides, obesity and adult onset (type 2) diabetes (<span>Lebeck 2014</span>). It may be a drug target for anti-type 2 diabetes (<span>M&eacute;ndez-Gim&eacute;nez <em>et al.</em> 2018</span>). AQP-7- and AQP-9-mediated glycerol transport in tanycyte cells may be under hormonal control to use glycerol as an energy source during the mouse estrus cycle (<span>Yaba <em>et al.</em> 2017</span>).&nbsp; It may also influence whole body energy metabolism (<span>Iena and Lebeck 2018</span>) including in the kidney (<span id="ref34556573.37277652" class="cite">Schlosser <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>). Aquaporin-7-mediated glycerol permeability is linked to human sperm motility in asthenozoospermia and during sperm capacitation (<span id="ref34557088.37566082" class="cite">Ribeiro <em>et al.</em> 2023</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Animals</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp7 of <em>Homo sapiens</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.7"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.7&tcname=">1.A.8.9.7</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC>Glycerol facilitator, Yf1054c (70.5 kDa protein) (<span id="ref3972.12832087" class="cite">Oliveira <em>et al</em>., 2003</span>)</TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC>Yeast </TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC>Yf1054c of <I>Saccharomyces cerevisiae</i> (P43549)</TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.8"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.8&tcname=">1.A.8.9.8</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Glycerol uptake facilitator of 393 aas</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Fungi</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Glycerol transporter of <em>Cordyceps militaris </em>(Caterpillar fungus)</p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#99ccff"><TD><b><A NAME="1.A.8.9.9"></A><A HREF="tcprotein.php?substrate=1.A.8.9.9&tcname=">1.A.8.9.9</a></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aquaporin/glycerol facilitator of 294 aas and 6 TMSs.&nbsp; May play a role in freeze tolerance (<span id="ref34544720.26402924" class="cite">Hirota <em>et al.</em> 2015</span>).</p></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC></TD><TD><b><font color=#3333CC><p>Aqp-9 of<em> Xenopus tropicalis</em></p></TD></TR><TR bgcolor="#ffffff" valign=top><TD COLSPAN=4 valign=top>&nbsp;</CENTER></TD></TR></TABLE>
